Discussion of the Election Process: According to the company's general manager, Jing Yimeng, this Standard Great Man Election has received celebrities from all walks of life, such as Cai Yuanpei, Pan Gongzhan, Wu Tiecheng's wife, Zhang Shouyong, Chen Guangfu, Yu Zuoting, Du Yuesheng, Wu Yun Chu, Wang Boyuan, Hu Pu'an, Yan Duhe, and the late Shi Liangcai, to generously serve as Standard Celebrity Electors. As for the enthusiastic participation of people from all walks of life in the election, it was even more unexpected.

Scholarship Distribution: Regarding the scholarship for the winners of the ordinary election, there is a total of 5,500 yuan for each. (A) The top 10 closest to the winner will each be awarded a university scholarship of 250 yuan per person. (B) The next top 10 closest to the winner will each be awarded a middle school scholarship of 150 yuan per person. Students will also receive book vouchers. The methods are: (A) Ten students who circled the winner completely will each receive a certificate from the Education Bureau and a 10-yuan book voucher from the China-America Tobacco Company. (B) The Education Bureau will publish an announcement for the 500 students who are closest to the winner, and the China-America Tobacco Company will each give a one-yuan book voucher. (C) The Education Bureau will issue a certificate to each of the top two schools with the most circled middle school students, and the China-America Tobacco Company will give a set of Kaiming's Twenty-Five Histories. (D) The Education Bureau will issue a certificate to each of the top two schools with the most circled elementary school students, and the China-America Tobacco Company will give a set of the Commercial Press's Young Children's Library.

Major Traffic Accidents Should Be Reported to the Ministry According to Regulations 131

The Lianglu Administration received instructions from the Ministry of Railways, stating: Regarding matters such as route obstructions, bridge damage, and train collisions occurring on various lines, the station where the incident occurred should telegraph the responsible bureau and simultaneously telegraph the Transportation Department of the Ministry. Furthermore, the Railway Bureau should telegraph the Ministry with detailed information within 24 hours. This was already communicated to all lines in the tenth month of the twentieth year to be followed. However, recently, after major accidents occurred on various lines, the stations involved often failed to notify the Transportation Department of the Ministry according to the regulations. This has resulted in the Ministry often being unable to promptly understand the true situation regarding major traffic accidents on various lines. Sometimes, newspapers in various locations have already published the information, while the Ministry has not yet received a detailed report. This situation is highly inappropriate. Therefore, the previous order is reiterated. In the future, if any major traffic accidents occur, the regulations established in the tenth month of the twentieth year must be strictly followed and must not be deliberately violated. In addition to issuing separate orders, this order is hereby issued for the bureau to follow. This bureau has already instructed the Engineering, Transportation, and Mechanical Departments, as well as the Police Department, to comply.

Team Leader Sworn into Office

Hongqiao Town in the Pu Song District of West Shanghai is strategically located, bordering Zhongshan Avenue to the east, Songjiang and Qingpu counties to the west, the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway to the south, and Hongqiao Road to the north. Ren Zuojun Returns to Shanghai After Investigating Life Insurance 133

The American Asiatic Life Insurance Company sent Mr. Ren Zuojun abroad in June last year to investigate the life insurance business. Mr. Ren has now returned to Shanghai. According to him, after going abroad, he engaged in research at the Maryland Life Insurance Company and the United Insurance Company in Baltimore, USA. Later, he conducted on-site research at the two largest insurance companies in New York. Each of these two insurance companies employs 12,000 clerks and 50,000 managers, making their scale unparalleled in the world. His research on life insurance focused on weekly savings and longevity insurance, and he gained a lot of insights. In addition to studying life insurance, he also investigated the conditions of various factories in the eastern United States, such as gasoline refineries, steel mills, sugar factories, bicycle manufacturing plants, fertilizer factories, and aircraft manufacturing plants, all of which he visited. He was particularly amazed by the grandeur of the Chicago World's Fair. After leaving the United States, he traveled through Europe, exited the Suez Canal, and returned to China via India. He paid attention to the industrial and commercial conditions of the countries he passed through, as well as the various political and economic facilities related to the welfare of the people. Furthermore, Mr. Ren traveled around the world and purchased meaningful landscape photos and several industrial samples for future exhibitions. However, he is currently too busy to sort them out. Once they are sorted out, they will be made public. Anyone who is interested in foreign industrial and commercial enterprises and wants to discuss with Mr. Ren to gain practical benefits can write directly to Mr. Ren (address: American Asiatic Life Insurance Company, Bund, Shanghai) to arrange a meeting.

Fire at Sanpailou Road 135

The rear building of Yongfengchang Cardboard Workshop at No. 64 Zhangjia Lane, Sanpailou Road in the city, was rented to a Ningbo old woman named Wang Shi, aged 40. At 3:25 PM yesterday, a fire broke out unintentionally. Suddenly, thick smoke billowed, and fierce flames soared. Furthermore, the cardboard workshop downstairs stored cardboard materials such as sulfur and rosin. Once ignited, the fire became uncontrollable and spread to the neighboring houses on both sides. It engulfed the Yuwanxing Clothing Store at No. 62 and the Yang family residence at No. 66, spreading to the east wing upstairs of No. 39 Fuxing Lane behind them. When the fire was raging, the North District Fire Brigade rushed to the scene with hose carts to put out the fire. It was not until after 5:00 PM that the fire was extinguished. A total of three buildings and the upstairs of one wing were burned down. The fire starter, Wang Shi, was immediately detained by the patrol police and taken to the Yemiao Police Station for punishment.

The Crew of the Jiahe Ship Were Ransomed Three Times Unsuccessfully 137

Bandits Ask for Ransom Payments in Different Tiers

Family Members Decide to Take Joint Action

Since the Jiahe ship of the China Merchants Bureau was robbed by pirates, the ship has been out of service. The pirate leader arranged for representatives of the families of the three kidnapped crew members to negotiate, but two attempts failed. Now, the third attempt has also broken down. The families of the three hostages have decided not to pay the ransom and let things take their course. The latest follow-up reports are as follows:

Contacted Three Times　During the second time that the representatives sent by the three crew members arrived in port to negotiate with the bandits, the bandits suddenly demanded a ransom of 60,000 yuan, making it impossible to pay, and the negotiations ended. At the beginning of last month, the bandits suddenly claimed that they were willing to automatically reduce the ransom for the three men and ordered the families to send representatives to the port again. The three families jointly appointed a Mr. Zhong as their representative to go to the port for the third negotiation to redeem the hostages. When Mr. Zhong arrived in port, he was hoping to redeem the three men, but to his surprise, another change occurred.

Bandits Ask for Different Prices　During the third negotiation with the bandits, the ransom prices for the three men were indeed reduced compared to the previous time, but the bandits changed the ransom prices for the three crew members to be different based on importance and seniority. This differed from the second time, where each person was 20,000 yuan. The ransom prices proposed by the bandits, at the lowest limit, were 10,000 yuan for business director Shen Qinxiang, 7,500 yuan for accountant Li Xiaobin, and, because his family was poor, 2,500 yuan for tallyman Ge Liangchen. When the representative, Mr. Zhong, departed from Shanghai, he only had 2,000 yuan prepared. When he heard the amount demanded by the bandits, the gap was too large, and no results were achieved.

Willing to Live and Die Together　Mr. Zhong sent a letter to the families informing them of the amounts. The families of Shen and Li decided not to pay the ransom and let things take their course, because they really did not have the financial resources and were not simply disregarding the situation. However, it was heard that Ge Liangchen's ransom was the lowest. The families of Shen and Li told Ge Liangchen's family that since the three were kidnapped together, they should be united. If a ransom was paid, then all three should be redeemed. Even if the bandits reduced the price for one of the three to 200 yuan, they could not act independently to pay the ransom. They are determined to live and die together and have instructed Mr. Zhong not to continue negotiations and have decided to let things take their course. It has been more than three months since Shen, Li, and Ge were kidnapped.

The Chongqi Merger Movement is Actively Underway 138

Yesterday, Reporters Were Invited to Report on the Progress

And Urge the Government to Merge Chongqi as Soon as Possible

The Chongqi merger movement was launched by the Chongming Shanghai Association, which yesterday invited the press to the Atlantic Restaurant on Simalu to explain the origins of the merger movement and its progress. Among those in attendance were the association's committee members Lu Caifu, Wu Caichen, Yang Zhenzhong, Shi Chongpeng, Lu Yinchu, Xu Peihang, Shi Rongruo, Lu Xizhen, Chen Dongbai, and more than 30 reporters from various newspapers. The details are recorded as follows:

Chairman's Report　Chairman Shi Fujiu reported, saying that the discussion of dividing Chongming to found the county of Qidong began in the early years of the Republic of China. Shi Zipei, a native of Haimen living in Waisha, repeatedly requested the division of the county, but the provincial authorities did not allow it. In the eighth year, representatives from Waisha jointly discussed solutions at the Shanghai Daoyin Office, such as adding an administrative committee for Waisha, a judicial trial officer, and dividing grain collection. Everything that could benefit the people of Waisha was taken into account, and the people of Waisha have been living in peace for a long time. However, in the seventeenth year, the county was suddenly divided, which led to a sharp increase in government expenses and land taxes, causing the people to suffer greatly. The Chongming Shanghai Association, therefore, united fellow townsmen from various places to organize the Chongqi Merger Movement and has received guidance from many gentlemen. If Chongqi is merged, 800,000 people will be able to see the light of day again.

Telegraph to the Government　To the Executive Yuan, Ministry of Interior, Ministry of Finance, and Governors of the Jiangsu Province of the National Government: This humble submission is made because we, the people of Chongming, have suffered under harsh government for a long time. This small, remote area has been divided into two counties, which has sharply increased taxes and seriously burdened the people's livelihood. Hunger and thirst plague them, and they exhaust their income and deplete their land to satisfy the insatiable appetite of those in power. The only recourse is to appeal for the swift abolition of the divided Qidong County and the correction and merger of the two areas. Only then can we strengthen the foundation and reduce waste, return politics to normalcy, recuperate and rejuvenate, and relieve the people from their distress. Otherwise, the destitute and abandoned will have no one left to rely on. Having witnessed the suffering of the people and the concerns of the homeland since the division of the county seven years ago, we feel it is our duty to break our silence and submit this summary to your consideration. The planning and demarcation of the country's territory has never been immutable. It is only by understanding the terrain, accurately assessing the people's sentiments, considering the financial capacity, and examining the actual needs that we can determine the direction of reform. In this way, the government can avoid missteps, and the people can avoid grievances. Chongming is an isolated island in the sea. The tides rise and fall, and sand accumulates to form continents. The sea changes into land, and the changes are unpredictable. Since the establishment of the prefecture in the Yuan Dynasty and the establishment of the county in the early Ming Dynasty, the city has been moved five times, and rumors have spread. It has been a time of anxiety and disintegration, but fortunately, the inner and outer sandbanks have grown together, complementing each other, and have been able to barely support themselves. Moreover, the so-called outer sandbanks are all people from our inner county who have braved the dangers of wind and waves and have worked tirelessly, carrying baskets and shovels, to cultivate the wasteland into fertile land. Every inch of land belongs to the people of Chongming, and it is their blood and sweat. Taking advantage of the natural terrain and making up for it with human effort, they have spent years and generations to build this land of Canaan, where they farm their fields, live in their houses, sing and cry. How can we bear to watch it being divided like a melon? The people of Chongming grow up by the sea and rarely see outsiders. The scholars value old virtues, and the farmers follow their ancestral customs. They are content and law-abiding, striving to be good citizens. Each has his share of farming, and there is no master-slave mentality. The amount of rent depends on the harvest, and they only know the joy of farming and do not hear the quarrels of sparrows and mice. The outer sandbanks regard the inner county as their old home, and the inner county regards the outer sandbanks as their new home. They help each other like fish forgetting each other in the rivers and lakes for a long time. There is no distinction between Chu and Han, but suddenly there is talk of drawing a dividing line, which is self-inflicted trouble and not what the people of Chongming want. Moreover, since the division of the county, the most difficult and unsolvable problem has been the financial problem. Before the division, the total budget of the county was only over 89,000 yuan, but after the division, the remaining old county of Chongming alone increased to over 489,000 yuan. Although Qidong is newly built, it is still equipped with everything it should have, increasing to over 449,000 yuan. The total has increased nearly twelve times. Even if there were copper mountains and cinnabar caves, they would be exhausted immediately. Can we say that a poor place like Chongming can bear this burden? According to the investigation, many provinces, prefectures, and counties have been abolished and merged after the reform. The most notable example is Wu County in Suzhou, which has merged two halls and three counties into one. The three Wu areas are rich and prosperous, far more so than Chongming, and yet they still implement abolition and merger to reduce waste. Chongming has a vast coastline and is not a strong county. Yet, it is forcing the people of one county to bear the government expenses of two counties. Anyone with common sense would say that this is impossible. Moreover, Chongming is a water town. In the past decade, it has been repeatedly attacked by typhoons and storm surges. Fields and villages have been engulfed by floods. Although the government has issued relief funds and charitable organizations have provided food and clothing, it is like a drop in the bucket, and the wounds are difficult to heal. Yet, huge government expenses are demanded from the dying victims, which is like asking for a crucian carp from a dried fish shop. There is no way to turn lead into gold or live on air. The strong are scattered in other places, and the weak fill the ravines. Even if one has the clever pen of the prison warden, it is difficult to describe the plight of displacement. Alas, what crime have the people of Chongming committed to face such anger? It is all because of the division of the county that they suffer this pain. For years, the elders in the villages have been running around, appealing for help, and their cries are not without reason. If the division of the county is necessary for practical reasons, then the people can endure temporary pain by destroying their homes to help, and enjoy happiness in the future. But after a careful examination of the facts, it turns out to be a big mistake. The establishment of the Republic is primarily to enlighten the people, so education is important. Those in Chongming who are in charge of education have always valued the principle of people's livelihood, treating the children of both inner and outer sandbanks equally, without any discrimination. However, the inner sandbanks have a dense population and more schools, while the outer sandbanks have sparse villages and fewer schools, but they have never stopped striving to popularize education. However, the education funds are all derived from the traditional academies and public fields, half of which are allocated by the village chiefs, and half of which are donated by the gentry and the wealthy. All of these are located in Qidong, so Chongming cannot reach them and does not receive a single drop, causing the schools to run out of food and the teachers to go hungry. Qidong is close to the water and can easily obtain resources, but they swallow everything up and leave nothing behind. Dwarfs measure the moon, and their hunger and satisfaction are different, and Chongming is already bankrupt. Recently, the rural areas have been depressed, and if we want to seek relief, we should start with dredging waterways and protecting dikes. Chongming's city is located on the coast and is in danger. In the late Qing Dynasty, the Guangxu Emperor specially allocated huge sums of money to build seawalls for defense. The village chiefs also drafted more than 5,000 acres of public fields and collected public rent specifically for annual repairs. These are also located in Qidong, but they have all been withheld, resulting in years of disrepair. It is difficult to ask the provincial treasury for repairs, and the thousands of residents near the city are in danger of being fish. Other charitable and infant care public fields in Qidong have also been seized. The villagers held the provincial government's proposal for equal division, and they argued on the basis of reason, but they were ignored. Moreover, eight years ago, Waisha proposed to run Baota, and the Yonglong Lianzhu merchants in both locations donated tens of thousands of yuan. After the establishment of the county, the money was all diverted, and no work was done. This is like raising the banner of dividing the county to carry out a deceptive scheme to seize public funds. Not only that, but the fields in Qidong are mostly the property of the people of Chongming. After the division of the county, the burden on the people of Chongming is already overwhelming. Every autumn harvest, they hope to collect the remaining ears of grain to supplement their income. Unfortunately, in the past two years, they have suffered from continuous drought and floods, and no grains have been harvested. However, the corrupt elements in Qidong still borrow from the government to pre-lend busy silver or pursue overdue taxes. If they do not comply, they will detain the landlords. On the other hand, they incite tenants to resist paying rent. Their methods are so vicious that they are alarming. This is not only borrowing the name of dividing the county to seize the public property of Chongming, but it is still not enough. They also plan to cut off the lifeblood of all the people of Chongming. This is a hidden worry about the hearts of the people and the world, and floods and wild beasts are not only a disaster for Chongming. Moreover, Chongming is suspended in a vast sea and is not connected to the mainland. It has always been known as a paradise. For three hundred years, it has never suffered from the plunder of soldiers and bandits. In recent years, however, traffic has gradually become more convenient, and ambushes are often heard. In the years of the Republic of China, in the 16th and 17th years, Waisha experienced police trouble. The people of the inner sandbanks asked for troops and transported weapons, not afraid of the trouble of supplying them. It was not long before it was suppressed. But after the division of the county, the boundaries became clear, and A blamed B, and no one was responsible. As a result, bandits and robbers were rampant in Qidong, and kidnappings were often heard, and sometimes they even affected Chongming. It is called the division of the county, but the security is even less guaranteed. The people of Chongming no longer have a day of peace and tranquility. Looking ahead, the worries are endless. In summary of the facts listed above, there is not only no need to divide the county, but the division causes disputes. According to statistics, since the establishment of Qidong, the cost of public and private funds has been more than three or four million, but nothing has been done to satisfy the people. The most obvious achievement is that a small number of founding heroes of the county have gathered their supporters, occupied the organs, colluded with corrupt elements, and suppressed the ignorant people. They have done everything they can to make money. They were once poor children, but now they are rich men. If the increased government expenses after the division are not borne by the people, then we can divide Chongming Island into dozens or hundreds of counties, and it can be left alone. If the taxes of the two counties are distributed equally after the division, and the income is measured to determine the expenditure, such as the story of Qianlong in the Qing Dynasty dividing the sand and returning it to the hall, and reducing the taxes according to the land, then it can also be done without saying anything. But now, although the county territory has been cut, the taxes have increased instead of decreasing. Chongming is exhausted, and Qidong is not full. On the map, the name of the county and prefecture is falsely increased, and the people are burdened with double exploitation. It should be a family, but it is harmful to both sides. Why is this so? If the proposal to divide the county originated from the people of Chongming, then it is a self-inflicted disaster, and there is no one to blame. But it was proposed by Shi Zipei and others from Haimen who lived in Qidong. It is a strange thing to steal the owner's seat and to do the cooking. What love do Shi and others have for Chongming to do such a crazy thing? It is also seen that most of the tenants in Waisha are stupid and uneducated, and they can be intimidated and coerced, and they can be tricked and manipulated. They do not avoid the suspicion of overstepping their authority and will choose the fat to eat. However, Shi and others are ignorant and reckless people from the countryside and are not worthy of deep reproach. It is a pity that the provincial government at the time was deceived and did not consider it. It hastily asked the National Government to approve the case in a blink of an eye, which is regrettable. At that time, the Minister of Civil Affairs in Changshu was Mao from Haimen. He had just taken office and did not know the suffering of the people. He saw the addition of a county magistrate as a child's play. How can we know that the establishment of an official and the division of duties is a major event related to the country's economy and the people's livelihood? How can we allow it to be done recklessly, showing a moment's bravery and causing endless disasters to the people? According to the meaning of the Spring and Autumn Period, it is difficult to escape the responsibility of the wise. If they have a compassionate heart, they should regret their momentary recklessness and the disaster that has caused the people's souls. They must change their plans and try to make amends late. Then, it will be like untying the bell that was tied, and they can help with the merger from within. In this way, the eating of the sun and the moon will not harm the Ming Dynasty. After the division of Chongqi, the representatives of the two counties have different positions, and their opinions are different. The documents they sue each other are more than an inch thick. However, what Chongming has stated is nothing more than the unsuitability of the local geography, history, human relations, and material resources for the division, which are all facts that cannot be forced. As for what Qidong holds, it is nothing more than the inconvenience of paying taxes and lawsuits, transportation, and the imperfection of education and security facilities. Although there are some one-sided reasons, all of these should gather the spirit of social cooperation to seek progress, and it is by no means that setting up more government offices can be effective. Moreover, they have already planned and set up such things as the Waisha Administrative Committee, the Separate Trial Court, the Grain Collection Counter, the Public Ferry, the Normal School, and the Popular Arts and Crafts Institute. They have all taken shape, but what is lacking is a magnificent county hall to embellish them. However, according to the outline of nation-building, the county unit is based on local autonomy. If we must adhere to our own opinions, and say that Chongming's inner and outer sandbanks have the danger of wind and waves, which is not conducive to the unification of one county, we are being too narrow-minded. Do we not see that Japan in the east and Dinghai in Dongyue, either connect several continents into one country or combine groups of islands into one county, and there is no danger of isolation? Chongming and Qidong are separated by only a strip of water, which can be crossed by a reed. How can there be a natural moat that cannot be crossed? In short, the people of Chongming are in distress because their livelihood is difficult, and if we add more overlapping organs to squeeze them, there will be a day of disintegration. We must strive to reduce consumption and increase production. They see the harm of the division as a pain in the flesh. Over the years, they have selected representatives who have spoken themselves hoarse, and have knocked on the doors to submit their petitions. Fortunately, they have received a letter from President Jiang, which was sent to the provincial government for consideration. The letter stated that if the division is convenient, the original plan should be maintained. If it is not suitable, then even if the plan is determined, it should be corrected. This shows that you have a high-hanging mirror and understand the situation. You have swept away the gloom and revealed the light of day, giving the people of Chongming great comfort. Generally speaking, in the Republic, the will of the people is the basis for all decisions. What is convenient for the people will be implemented with all our efforts, and what is not suitable for the people will be changed immediately. We have translated the President's letter, and the merger of Chongqi is purely based on interests, without adhering to the established practice. Now, the harm of the division has been recognized, and it is necessary to correct it quickly. The people are suffering in a foreign land, and they are attached to their hometown. They cannot bear to watch their 800,000 fathers, elders, brothers, and brothers sink into the depths of suffering without lending a helping hand. Therefore, we have specially listed the various hardships and difficulties after the division, and especially the financial aspect, which is very important. Hundreds of thousands of yuan of the people's hard-earned money are spent every year to fill the pockets of the local corrupt officials, which only causes division and does not help the local area. If this is not changed, it will be difficult to continue. This makes the people of Chongming unable to sleep in peace, and they have to express their feelings fully. We have always admired your compassion and care for the people, and you must lift us out of the fire and put us on the mat. We humbly request that you examine and approve the reasons for the unsuitability of the division of Chongqi and correct the original plan by abolishing Qidong County to conform to the President's letter and the suffering of the people of Jiangsu. We are in a state of fear and trembling. We hope that you will consider this carefully. The Chongqi Merger Promotion Committee, Chairman Cao Yinqiu, Standing Committee Members Lu Caifu, Gong Jianqiu, Tong Hangbai, Qu Runchu, Lu Yanghao, Shi Fujiu, Lu Yinchu, Yang Zhenzhong, Committee Members Wu Caichen, Xu Peihang, Chen Dongbai, Qu Zhibu, Tang Yujiu, Chen Xiangxin, Tong Muge, Song Lifeng, Yang Songyu, Guo Xiuyan, Gong Pixiong, and others, 55 people in total.

Zhu Xingli's Mental Illness Led to Suicide by Jumping from a Building 141

Zhu Xingli (age 27, from Zhenjiang), an employee of the Guanghua Petroleum Company, located on the fourth floor of the China Industrial Bank at No. 14 Museum Road, suddenly jumped from the window of the building at 9:30 last night. His head struck the ground, shattering his skull, and his blood gushed out like a spring. Fortunately, a passerby noticed and reported it to the police station. An ambulance was dispatched, and he was rushed to Renji Hospital for treatment. However, his brain was already shattered, and he died en route. The hospital notified the police, who transferred the body to the coroner's office. His family has already arrived at the hospital. According to them, Zhu had a history of mental illness, and this suicide by jumping was likely caused by a relapse.

Japanese Residents in China Resent the Shanghai and Manchurian Incidents 142

Japanese Residents in Shanghai Face Extreme Hardship

According to the Manchuria Daily on the 21st, last year's trade between Shanghai and Japan saw a significant import surplus for Japan, which greatly impacted the financial world. Although the Nanjing government has been working hard to prevent the outflow of silver, Shanghai is critically short of hard currency, further tightening the financial situation. In addition, the rural areas along the Yangtze River have been affected by drought, significantly reducing purchasing power. The Shanghai market is overflowing with inventory. There are 30,000 Japanese residents in Shanghai. Aside from those living on salaries, the rest are experiencing extreme hardship. As a result, complaints and curses about the Manchurian and Shanghai incidents are rife. In Nanjing, there are only 130 Japanese residents, mostly consulate staff and news reporters, with no individually-owned businesses. The situation for Japanese residents in Shandong is also very bleak. In short, the current situation of Japanese residents in China is similar to the poverty experienced in Manchuria in January of the sixth year of the Showa era.

However, the internal situation of the bank is still unclear to outsiders. It is said that the bank's shareholders are all reputable merchants with substantial shares. They are now comprehensively planning the liquidation process, both collecting debts and repaying liabilities, and also seeking to realize assets to ease his burden as the person in charge of liquidation. He will handle the liquidation seriously, taking into account the credit of the shareholders and protecting the interests of the creditors. An examination of the bank's assets and liabilities shows that they are balanced, but some assets are illiquid. In this economic downturn, selling them will take time. He asks all creditors for their understanding and patience while awaiting a resolution. As for depositors, they will be paid out proportionally as soon as the cash is collected.

Letter to the Editor 150

To the esteemed editor of Shen Bao,

Having read yesterday’s (26th) report in your newspaper from the Japanese News Alliance, regarding Jin Bofan, representative of the Shanghai International Trade Association, arriving in Kobe. The report stated: “The Shanghai National Federation of Commerce, representing the interests of the Chinese people’s businesses, has dispatched Jin Bofan, General Manager of the International Enterprise Company, as a special envoy to Japan to investigate concrete plans for economic cooperation between China and Japan, in order to express mutual sincerity and make a statement, saying that our country’s industrial and commercial circles warmly welcome Japanese goods, etc.” We were greatly surprised to read this. Our association has always aimed to promote foreign trade, and we have never heard of Jin Bofan. Moreover, after carefully examining the content of the report, it claims that he was dispatched by the National Federation of Commerce (note: the National Federation of Commerce has also denied this, as seen in today’s issue of your newspaper), which has nothing to do with our association, let alone bear the title mentioned in the report. This is clearly a mistake, and we fear that it will cause misunderstandings in all circles. We hereby send this letter to request a correction.

Sincerely,

China International Trade Association

February 27th

Free Talk

Mutual Generation of Sentiment and Writing 151

— Li Tongyu

When I used to read books annotated by Jin Shengtan, I often saw the phrase "sentiment generates writing, writing generates sentiment," but I didn't quite understand its true meaning. In recent years, as I've learned to write, my thoughts naturally flow from under my pen halfway through, and the meaning of the entire piece is mostly something I hadn't thought of when I started writing. Sometimes when I'm writing a novel, I change the content of the original planned story halfway through, and create a new plan based on what comes to me as I write. As a result, someone I originally intended to write as a villain might end up being a good person, and someone I intended to write as a good person might turn into a bad one. Developing the story along with the new meaning that arises from the writing allows the entire story to be seamless without a single crack. Of course, you can achieve the greatest success by writing the characters according to a predetermined plan, but you must have extremely deep cultivation and be able to grasp the characters under your pen, not to be moved by the new realm created by the writing, that is, to grasp the writing so that it does not create a new realm beyond the original plan. Otherwise, the whole piece will appear stiff and unnatural. This is the effect of "mutual generation of sentiment and writing."

Therefore, sometimes when we don't intend to write a long, brilliant article, but just think of an idea and write arbitrarily, we can write something quite good. Similarly, sometimes when we are full of confidence that we will write a valuable masterpiece, we abandon the unfinished manuscript halfway through and cannot continue. The former is because our writing generates new situations (or moods), while the latter only has dead situations (or moods) and cannot generate living writing. This is also the effect of "mutual generation of sentiment and writing."

Those engaged in writing cultivation must train their writing to suit the intended atmosphere of the entire piece, and this atmosphere will evoke "sentiment," which is precisely what helps the development of "writing." "Mutual generation of sentiment and writing" without exceeding the scope of the intended content of an article is a necessary condition for completing a good work. But how easy is it to talk about!

When Alexandre Dumas fils wrote the script for La Dame aux Camélias, he forgot that this pitiful woman was a character created by his own pen, so he cried first when he wrote about the death of Camille. The Japanese female writer Hirabayashi Taiko, she cried while writing a novel, cried and then wrote, wrote and then cried, these are just examples I grabbed at random. I believe that no literary masterpiece is written without this kind of thing.

If the author is not moved by the characters they create, the condition of "mutual generation of sentiment and writing" cannot be achieved.

Heart Talk 152

— Ding

Every year at the end of the year and the beginning of the new year, my heart is often stirred up by various changes. On the one hand, I really feel that time passes too quickly, and this causes deep annoyance in my heart. Firstly, I am getting older, and people are gradually aging, and I have achieved nothing in my career! But after the beginning of spring, my thoughts change again, and my heart seems to become active. At times like these, I always like to say to myself: "Let the past roll away! The future should be properly invigorated, work hard! Restart my work, do not waste precious time and squander my limited life!"

After saying this, there was indeed a time when I was "single-mindedly" and "buried myself in my work" and my heart was stirred for a considerable time. But soon after, I gradually cooled down, until I relaxed into laziness.

This is how one year after another passed.

Although I can't say that I am old now, or how decadent and bored, I am not like a young man with vigor.

I think: This is because I am lazy, unfortunately sad, where failure lies, and the reason why I am crushed into the soil behind the giant wheels of the times. Because of my opportunistic and idle attitude, I have suffered a lot of losses. As soon as things come, when I feel that my knowledge is shallow, my skills are low, and my application is not enough, I feel so regretful, sad, uncomfortable, and sorry. ... But what's the use of this?

All the facts make me ashamed. Although I can say in good conscience that I am not a hopeless person, and I have indeed done some things with hardship. But this is so small.

Move forward, the past is only a few steps to start. Move forward, carrying my heart that has been cultivated with blood, and move forward silently.

Life should be full of fire. I hate my life force without the light of fire. However, I hope that I can really do something from now on. Bravely overcome my general bad habits and slip into the giant wheel of the century.

Slip in until life reaches the last breath.

Slip in until life reaches the last drop of blood.

Human life will continue forever without interruption.

The course of time will continue to advance without stagnation.

It is the evolution of endless progress!

I think from taking fire from diamonds to inventing matches, from oil lamps to electric lights, from running and taking boats to cars, trains, steamships, and airplanes; from caves and huts to high-rise buildings, from raw food to cooked food, miscellaneous food; from leaves, hemp, and leather to silk, satin, and damask ... I don't know how much time has passed and how many lives have been sacrificed to succeed.

This is the product of cultural progress, the accumulation of valuable human experience and the crystallization of wisdom. Although these materials cannot be enjoyed by the general public.

Therefore, I feel that everyone should be committed to culture. I feel that the working people are the true creators of culture.

I hope I can do this, and everyone can do this.

Settlement (Part Two) 153

— Xia Shi

Inside the house, there was a brazier, and Fourth Master was leaning on a rocking chair, warming himself with his woman. As usual, the ritual officer shouted upon entering:

"Fourth Master! Have you eaten?" His voice was unnatural.

Fourth Master's eyelids flickered upward, followed by a few coughs, as a greeting.

The ritual officer casually sat down on a stool. He placed the brazier at his feet, his eyes staring straight at the fire inside.

A silent moment. The ritual officer's face felt hot, and the words swirled in his throat. He came specifically to settle the account, and if he didn't speak, it wouldn't do. So, he steeled his heart and slowly forced the words out of his throat with effort.

"Master! Let's settle up?"

"..." The Master's eyelids flickered again. After a moment, he slowly propped himself up and went into the room.

He took the abacus in one hand and the ledger in the other, and brought them from the room to the square table in the hall. He turned on the light, flipped through the ledger, and the abacus rattled.

The ritual officer rolled his eyes.

The abacus stopped rattling, and suddenly, it seemed as if a thunderbolt had struck from nowhere, and the master shouted:

"Ritual officer! In the end, you still owe fifteen dollars!"

Fifteen dollars! The ritual officer was startled and stood up straight, stammering:

"Owe that much?"

"How much do you say you owe? This is recorded in the books." The master immediately became impatient and coughed a few times.

"I borrowed sixteen strings of cash; I did more than a dozen days of work, and there were a hundred bundles of weeds, the two offset..." The ritual officer was calculating in his head.

"Aren't you counting the owed rent grain?" The master quickly added.

"Owed rent grain? When did I owe it?" The ritual officer's voice was trembling.

"Don't you know?" The master coughed again, pointed to the ledger, and his attitude became more moderate. "Let me tell you! Last year you owed two shi of rent grain, and this year you owe two dou and one sheng of bean rent, right? The grain is calculated at four dollars per shi, with one year's interest, totaling nine dollars and sixty cents; the beans, including interest, are calculated at two dollars; after deducting your wages and weed money, it will be... There won't be any mistakes."

"The rent grain from last year, wasn't it already agreed to be waived? In those years!" The ritual officer suppressed his anger and his tone seemed like a plea.

"Is it that easy? Waiving two shi of grain in one go." The master laughed coldly and sat back on the rocking chair.

"The bean rent was also waived! This year there weren't even any bean seeds."

"..." The master closed his eyes, said nothing, and the only sound was the cold laughter coming from his nostrils.

"Deduct these two items. See how much I owe?" His tone became more earnest.

"..." Still only the cold laughter from his nostrils.

"That piece of land is too bad, I have to subsidize the rent every year, I won't farm it." The ritual officer couldn't hold back a little.

"You won't farm that piece of land?" The master opened his eyes and looked at him. His attitude remained leisurely.

"I won't farm it! I don't have the capital to subsidize it." The ritual officer replied resolutely.

"Really won't farm it?" The master still laughed from his nostrils.

"I won't!"

"Alright then! If you don't farm it, then don't farm any of the land! My land is well-matched, good and bad, I'd rather let it go to waste." The master stood up, picked up the ledger from the table, and walked back into the room.

The ritual officer was so angry that he couldn't breathe, and his hands and feet were shaking. After a long time, he shouted:

"Then I won't farm any of it! If I don't farm the land, will I starve to death?"

He grabbed the brazier and ran out.

He broke through the darkness and entered his own house. From inside the house, a ray of light leaked out, it was a green oil lamp, flickering dimly, and his woman was spinning cotton.

"Too evil! See if I starve to death!" He entered the room and sat down on the bed. His face was liver-colored, and his eyes were drooped down. He was panting, shouting louder and louder, as if crying.

His woman couldn't make heads or tails of it, and stared at him blankly.

"Why?"

"Damn it, too evil, I definitely won't farm the land next year!" The ritual officer only cared about shouting.

His woman seemed to understand somewhat, stood up, moved closer to him, and asked again:

"Why, Fourth Master..."

"That old guy is too evil, I definitely won't farm his land next year!" The ritual officer was still panting.

"Are you crazy? Always that ox-like temper. If you don't farm the land, what will you do? Blame yourself for being poor." His woman's tears were about to fall. Then, she smelled the smell of alcohol, and added:

"You're going to drink again, getting drunk like this."

"Who's drunk?" The ritual officer turned his eyes and stared at his woman, who was too muddled and didn't understand him. "The rent grain that was agreed to be waived last year, he's going to add interest and calculate it this year, can you bear it?"

His woman lowered her head, and her tears fell to the ground. "Blame yourself for being poor, can you make a fuss over him?" After saying that, she simply walked back to the stool where she was spinning cotton and sobbed.

"If I don't make a fuss, what then?" He has no humanity. He only sees money.

"I can't not farm, can I!" The woman sobbed more intensely.

The ritual officer stopped speaking, fell on the bed, and covered his head with both hands. At first, he was still stubbornly circling in anger, but eventually his panting gradually calmed down. His nerves, which had lost the ability to think, were awakened by his woman's crying. If he didn't farm the land, what would he do? Then he realized that ahead there was only a long and endless dark road, without sunshine, without farms, and filled only with wandering, hunger, and death. He couldn't help but sigh, and tears naturally followed.

"What will we do? What will we do?" He shouted crazily like a child. (The End)

Random Notes on Historical Anecdotes (7) 154

— Cao Juren

This section of narrative singing, in accordance with the original meaning of the Analects, expands on the conversations between the Southern hermits (Jieyu, Changju, Jieni) and Confucius's disciples with added details and embellishments. Not only is it vividly lifelike and modernized, but the meaning of the whole text is also modernized. Storytellers after the Song and Yuan dynasties and novelists who wrote chapters of novels mostly excelled in embellishment. There are teahouses where the story of a young lady instructing her maid can last for a month, which can be said to be the ultimate in embellishment. Recently, the translated text of the Analects by Mr. Juesheng, serialized in volumes 12, 1, 2, and 3 of the Guowen Weekly, also uses the method of embellishment, such as translating "The ancients did not speak rashly, fearing that they would not be able to do it themselves" as "Ancient people did not shout slogans randomly, afraid that they would not be able to do it themselves." Translating "A gentleman helps those in need, not those who are already rich" as "I would rather send charcoal in the snow than spread oil on fat!" are all very well embellished. ("Embellishment" originally meant "to extend its meaning," but now it is misused, and is interpreted as "dealing with it carelessly.")

"Embellishment" can be said to be a rough and broad effort. Further, I will talk about another kind of delicate effort, namely the so-called "rendering method." The predecessors created many lyrical texts, describing farewells. Jiang Yuantong's "Farewell Fu", the first paragraph reads:

"...Therefore, the traveler's intestines are broken, a hundred feelings are sad, the wind whistles with strange sounds, the clouds are vast with strange colors, the boat is frozen on the shore, the carriage is slowly moving on the side of the mountain; the oars are still, but do not move forward, the horse is cold and neighing without rest! ... The residents lie down in sorrow, as if something is lost, the sun sets against the wall, casting a sinking color, the moon rises above the eaves, spreading flying light..."

The following section describes farewells of the rich and powerful, farewells of chivalrous people, farewells of soldiers, farewells of those going to remote countries, farewells of couples, farewells of those outside the world, and farewells of those in the brothels, which are described in separate paragraphs. This theme, when it came into the hands of the Northern Song Dynasty lyricist Liu Yong, took on a new appearance. He used various methods to write about the essence of farewell, and each was different, such as in "Rain Bells":

"Cicadas chirping mournfully; facing the long pavilion in the evening, the sudden rain has just stopped. At the city gate, I have no mood for a farewell feast, reluctant to part, the orchid boat urges its departure. Holding hands and looking at each other with tearful eyes, I am speechless and choking... Affection has always been saddened by farewells; how can I bear the desolation of this clear autumn season! Where will I wake up tonight? On the willow bank, in the dawn wind and the remaining moon!..."

He never uses stories to pile up, but renders an exterior view to construct a psychological picture, which is by no means something that Jiang Yuantong's rough method could write. Later, when it came into the hands of Northern Qu writers, it was even more different. Such as Dong Jieyuan's "Romance of the Western Chamber", a folding fan of parting at the Long Pavilion:

"...The rain has just stopped, the evening wind is as cold as ice, and the sound of decaying willows and cicadas is mournful! I don't know when we will see each other again after today's parting? On the sleeves, tears are wiped away, lingering without end, and the secret knot of hatred is hidden on the brow, so difficult to give up, even if there are thousands of kinds of emotions, where to say it? Do not say that a man's heart is like iron stone, you can't see the red leaves all over the river, all are the blood in the eyes of the people who are separated!... The decayed grass is sad and leads to a single path, and the red maple leaves are scattered and full of the forest. There are no fixed traces in his life, like broken weeds, listening to the cold geese flying across the heavy twilight clouds. I remember the mandarin duck quilt, tonight the half wall is useless. The sight is full of thousands of kinds of sorrow; seeing the red leaves dripping and flowing, the pitter-patter of the light rain, the rustling of the west wind! The donkey whip is half swayed, the shoulders are shrugged, do not ask how light or heavy the parting sorrow is, on the horse, even the camel can't move it!"

Towards Evening (9) 155

— Qu Yi

"It's nothing, nothing at all." Hu Yiyuan plopped down on the sofa. At the same time, he invited the two of them to sit on the two chairs near the entrance. "Old friends should meet often! Get a room, take a bath, and have a chat while we're at it—"

Since there was nothing to discuss, coming here was just a waste of time. The two men hadn't expected this turn of events, so they were a little dazed. They managed dry smiles, casually looking around the room. Then, they all noticed the potbelly standing by the corner of the table — a large belly wrapped in a radiant white homespun short shirt and pants.

"Oh!" Hu Yiyuan stood up again. The introductions began. "This is my distant maternal uncle. He's a man of divisional commander caliber. —And this one, oh! He was my classmate during the Japanese occupation, a classmate at the East Asia Preparatory University. A new writer. —This one, hey, my uncle, don't let his short stature fool you; he's a national walking hero! Truly rare, truly rare."

"Hahaha!" Following the introduction, there was a burst of laughter, indicating mutual "sincere unity." "Hahaha!"

Then, silence returned to the room. A snow-like white light shimmered before everyone's eyes. They exchanged knowing smiles again — starting to "be humorous." However, before long, the new writer finally broke the "humor," bowing to the potbelly;

"To which army does your esteemed self belong?" he asked affably.

The potbelly seemed to have been silenced, unable to respond. In uneasy anxiety, he kept turning his belly like a globe, turning, turning. "No, no, no," a drum-like sound leaked out, one syllable at a time.

Clear breeze, fine rain, red mud temple, no monks returning, only swallows.

Shen Bao Domestic Goods Weekly

Words of Contribution

Public Education and Domestic Goods 156

— Yun Xun

Twenty years ago, the term "public education" seemed not to exist yet, but the clamor to promote domestic goods was already quite loud and familiar. Public education in cities started building earlier, but the actual effects were not significantly improved, and the benefits to the unschooled masses were barely noticeable. I think the problem lies in the four words "aiming too high." If one diligently seeks practical work, those running public education would definitely not feel the current gloom.

Public education centers are now common in every county and relatively prosperous market town, but upon entering these places, one only sees a few daily newspapers, several kinds of magazines, plant specimens, and the usual colored birds, animals, insects, as well as some physiological models. What else? One can't find anything else. These displays have become the cliché of public education centers, the self-evident duty of those running public education. Year after year, year after year, the scope of public education seems to be like the textbooks compiled and reviewed by the Ministry of Education. I'm not saying that plant and animal specimens, physiological models, etc., are not suitable materials for the public to increase their general knowledge, but I think they are too rigid, not the expression of a progressive nation. Gentlemen serving in public education centers! Don't treat it as something for eating and sleeping, it is a sharp weapon for completing an excellent national character! Public education should be regarded as a movement. In addition to smoking and chatting, spend more time in the office, use your brains to think of ideas, what should be promoted, what should be abolished. We often see many public education centers treating the dignified office as a club for a few staff members, with string and bamboo instruments, singing and chanting to their hearts' content, like a "nursing home." They treat it as a small yamen directly under the Education Bureau, working, resting, looking lively.

I hope the education authorities will add a "Domestic Goods Exhibition Room" to each public education center, carefully selecting local products, guiding the audience to distinguish trademarks. Over the years, local men, women, old and young will recognize the products of their county and promote them to neighboring counties. The local products of neighboring counties are transported to this county. Such a constant flow of displays will naturally deepen the Chinese people's impression of domestic goods day by day. Everyone knows that holding domestic goods exhibitions requires dedicated venues, dedicated personnel, and is only temporary, which is not within the financial reach of every small county. This year is the Student Domestic Goods Year. To be honest, the visitors to the public education center are mostly people from the education sector and students. It is better to first display educational supplies, and then include household daily clothing, food, and drink. Building the public's awareness of domestic goods seems to be closer and more relevant than imparting other general knowledge. It will not waste government funds and will strengthen the national economic front. Let's not "aim too high"! Let's do it practically.

Talking About Textbook Problems 157

— Xin Quan

In schools, the most contact students have is naturally with books. Because, not counting class time, and after school, self-study, they almost always stay with books. From this, we can see the close relationship between books and general students. But here is the issue, at present, nine out of ten textbooks supplied to students by major bookstores are printed on foreign paper. In the Student Domestic Goods Year, students are actually reading books printed on foreign paper. Isn't this a completely contradictory thing? But in modern bookstores, to find a book printed on domestic paper, except for old-style thread-bound Four Books and Five Classics, it can be said that "it simply doesn't exist." If schools use the Four Books and Five Classics as textbooks, of course, it is impossible. Isn't this a deadlock? To read, one can only use textbooks printed on foreign paper. If one is willing to drop out of school because of not using foreign goods, it would be like abandoning eating for fear of choking, which seems too clumsy.

In fact, the solution to this problem is simply for a few bookstores that supply textbooks to switch to using domestic paper for printing! However, most bookstores have already printed the books used in the spring. If they want to switch to using domestic paper for printing, it would be difficult to do so temporarily due to cost considerations. Therefore, this problem seems difficult to solve. But we should not let it take its own course simply because it is "difficult."

The "Student Domestic Goods Year" has begun not long ago! We certainly hope that it can achieve good results this year and occupy the most glorious page in the Domestic Goods Year. Therefore, I am happy to bring up this textbook problem and discuss a suitable solution with the managers of various bookstores and the headmasters of schools so that general students can achieve the goal of "students not using foreign goods for anything" in this Domestic Goods Year.

After the Domestic Goods Survey 158

— Jiang Yan

Ink

Domestic Goods — Minsheng 32%, Dahua 27%, Other 2% Total 61%

Non-Domestic Goods — Huatuomen 20%, Biande 14%, Paike 3%, Other 2% Total 39%

Pencils

Domestic Goods Pencils — Dahua 75%

Non-Domestic Goods Pencils — 25%

Domestic Goods Fountain Pens — Boshi 12%, Guan Lemin 9%, Other 8% Total 29%

Non-Domestic Goods Fountain Pens — Paike 35%, Kangkeling 20%, Other 16% Total 71%

Paper (Including Exercise Books, Stationery, Draft Paper, etc.)

Domestic Goods — 30% Non-Domestic Goods — 70%

In our middle school of five hundred people, I spent three days running through classrooms and dormitories and made the above survey report. This time, I only took paper, ink, and pencils as the scope. The purpose is to know in our Student Domestic Goods Year, where have these most important "Four Treasures of the Study" reached now? That is, what achievements have our students made in rejecting non-domestic "Four Treasures of the Study?" Although my survey cannot be entirely accurate, and because of space constraints, I cannot divide it carefully, I firmly believe that this cannot but be considered an epitome of the beginning of the Student Domestic Goods Year.

I am very pleased that domestic pencils account for 75% of pencils, and ink accounts for 61%. At the same time, I also suspect that imported fountain pens actually occupy a position of 71% among them. Of course, a large part was bought before, but in the Student Domestic Goods Year, we have to consider this a big black spot. Domestic paper accounts for 30%, which I think is too little. Although everyone knows that the production of domestic paper is small, there has never been news of it being sold out. Therefore, I hope that its percentage will gradually be above that of imported goods.

Now let's calculate the average. It's very simple. We find that domestic goods account for 40% and imported goods account for 51%. I have thought that this difference of 2%, or even the entire 51%, is the weakness of our Student Domestic Goods Year. From this weakness, a country can suffer from a very dangerous anemia.

In short, the burden of the Student Domestic Goods Year is heavy, and this burden needs to be borne by all the people.

The Student in the Student Domestic Goods Year 159

— Ba Ling

"Promoting domestic goods, of course, is not limited to men and women, but the responsibility of students is especially important. Therefore, promoting domestic goods must start with students." These words are what I often talk about with people.

Why should promoting domestic goods start with students? Because students are the backbone of society, the pillars of the country. Their knowledge is rich, their hearts are pure, their emotions are fervent, and their actions are courageous. What society and the country expect of students is also very sincere. If promoting domestic goods can be entrusted to young students, I think there will definitely be considerable achievements.

Last year was the Women's Domestic Goods Year officially designated by various organizations. Although the results of the women's efforts cannot fully satisfy us, their contribution to publicity and advocacy, as well as the invisible reduction of the number of excess imports, is indelible. Someone said, "Women's abilities are ultimately inferior to men's, so the achievements ultimately cannot have significant expression." However, just how much higher are men's abilities than women's, or whether women's abilities are truly inferior to men's, is not only an educational problem but also a big problem between men and women, which can be set aside here. At the same time, from another perspective, this year is the Student Domestic Goods Year officially designated by various organizations. Although there are also female students participating in the student population, male students still account for the absolute majority. Therefore, how will the results of this year's Student Domestic Goods Year be? It can be regarded as a touchstone for whether men's abilities are higher than women's.

Dear young students, your great mission must begin to be borne from today! I very much hope that you will bravely accept it and have the determination that "promoting domestic goods is my sole responsibility." Whether it's clothing, food, or use... etc., you must choose to buy domestic goods, and you must not be sloppy anymore. You must know that students are the role models of society. If students can conscientiously use domestic goods, then, since people are inclined to do good, who is not like me? The general public will naturally be able to change their views, and this great effect of changing customs and habits will truly be attributed to the lovely and respectable young students.

Good, this year is the Student Domestic Goods Year, let the students do it! Here, I pre-wish the Student Domestic Goods Year success.

Domestic Goods News of the Week 160

The Ministry of Foreign Affairs, in order to promote trade in domestic goods in Southeast Asia and improve the lives of overseas Chinese, has specially sent Chen Shoupou, Liang Yugao, and Zheng Lin to Southeast Asia for inspection. Mr. Chen and others sent a special letter to Wu Zhihao, a member of the Standing Committee of the China National Products Production and Sales Association, soliciting the opinions of various manufacturers. Mr. Wu replied with six points: (1) setting up commercial attachés, (2) opening domestic goods exhibition halls, (3) establishing domestic goods promotion agencies, (4) establishing banks in various ports in Southeast Asia, (5) laying shipping routes, (6) mutual inspections at home and abroad.

Xue Shouchan, a silk magnate in Wuxi, recognizing the decline of China's silk industry and the sluggishness of exports, will depart soon to inspect the silk industries of the United States, France, Germany, and Japan for learning. He is scheduled to return home in eight months.

Rong Zongjing, the general manager of Shenxin Textile Company, believing that the development of the Japanese textile industry is worthy of learning, has specially sent Hui Zhidao and Zou Ruchui to Japan for inspection.

The International Trade Bureau is scheduled to convene more than 30 weaving factory owners in this city at 3:00 PM today (28th) to discuss ways to promote domestic bleached cloth to Southeast Asia.

The Domestic Goods Movement Boost Conference initiated earlier by the China National Products Manufacturers Association has now applied to the party and government agencies for record-keeping and has borrowed the open space of the Penglai Market as the venue. It is scheduled to officially open on March 15th.

The Wuxi National Exhibition initiated by the China National Products Factories Association has now found the old site of the National Products Market on Gongyuan Road as the venue. The opening ceremony is scheduled to be held tomorrow (1st). The exhibition period is set for about three weeks.

The Ministry of Industry, in order to promote domestic goods, has re-stipulated tax exemption and reduction measures for domestic goods exhibits. However, the certificate must be obtained from the Ministry. Yesterday, it has consulted the Shanghai Municipal Government for verification.

The Special Committee of the Mechanical Engineering Association held its first meeting on the 23rd, first studying the content of the regulations for the management of automotive machinery, and publicly elected Cai Shengbai and others as conveners.

The Shaoxing National Exhibition was originally scheduled to open on March 1st, but due to insufficient preparation, it has been postponed to March 5th. More than 50 companies have registered. In addition, the Anhui Province Wutun Road Along-the-Line Products Exhibition will also open soon, promoting along the road.

My Plan for the Student Domestic Goods Year 161

— Quan Jia

After the Women's Domestic Goods Year, it is our turn for the Student Domestic Goods Year. Some people may think that the foreign goods used by students are very limited. Speaking of the books they read, if they are only published abroad, they have to buy them. Why necessarily name it the Student Domestic Goods Year? I think that students are the masters of China, and their every move in the future will have a great impact on the rise and fall of the country. If they have a recognition of domestic goods in the current era of schooling, then China's national industry may be revitalized even more in the future. For this reason, I will write this plan.

1. Start with oneself: At present, people who generally promote domestic goods wear foreign goods and persuade people everywhere to use domestic goods. Do you think that this kind of person who cares only about words and not actions can do this work? Starting with oneself, in addition to promoting domestic goods by oneself, one can also reform the inferior habit of society using foreign goods. If the manager wears domestic clothes and a domestic hat, then the staff members will also have to use domestic goods.

2. Introduce domestic goods: In addition to using domestic goods oneself, one must also introduce them to people who do not know that there are domestic substitutes. For example, if you see your friend using a foreign fountain pen, you should respectfully say to him: "Brother, the Guan Lemin and Xinmin fountain pens of Chinese goods are indeed almost the same as foreign products, and the price is not expensive. China National Products Company has them for sale." Then, invisibly, you have helped the revitalization of domestic goods.

3. Visit domestic goods factories: This year, I hope to visit domestic goods factories more in my spare time. First, I can understand the lives of the domestic goods industry, and second, I can increase my knowledge. This is of great significance.

4. Read more books about domestic goods and write more articles about domestic goods: I plan to buy more books about the national domestic goods industry situation in various places, and customs statistics on the import and export of domestic and foreign goods. The former will make me understand the real situation, and the latter will let me know the success or failure of the domestic goods movement. Therefore, I will write many feelings into articles.

The above four points are my personal plan. I hope that students will cooperate and do a solid job. I also hope that I will not be all talk and no action and not persevere in doing it. Then, on the last day of this year, in my own diary, I will write: "Although I am still the same this year, there has been some achievement in the domestic goods work. The number of factories visited has reached fourteen. Thanks to the enthusiastic guidance of the various factories, I have benefited a lot. The domestic goods discussion group has been established for several months and the results are very good. The members have worked hard to cooperate, and there are many sponsors. However, the direction of progress needs to be discussed next year." At that time, how happy I should be!

"Wealth and Honor to Old Age" 162

— Mi Gao

"Having wealth and resources to enjoy wealth and honor, having a virtuous wife to grow old together." This is, of course, the supreme happiness in life. People toil and busy themselves all day long, nothing more than for this purpose.

But in these times of national hardship and social unrest, how many people can enjoy such perfect happiness? Aren't most people still dying prematurely in suffering?

Like Mr. Xiang Songmao, a well-known figure in China's industrial circles, he originally had a happy family, but he was tragically killed during the "January 28th" Shanghai Incident! However, although Mr. Xiang did not enjoy the happiness of "wealth and honor to old age," his death was for the country—for saving people. This spirit of sacrifice is truly great! His name can be immortalized forever; no wonder that when the third anniversary of Mr. Xiang's martyrdom was held this year, the people who participated were all moved to tears.

The Wuzhou Gu Ben Soap Factory has a kind of exquisite soap, the name of which is "Wealth and Honor to Old Age Soap." I think this name contains a profound meaning, and this meaning hints: promoting domestic goods can enrich the country and make the people prosperous. If everyone can purchase and use domestic goods, then profit rights will no longer flow out, the social economy will be stable, and people will all have the opportunity to enjoy perfect happiness.

Finally, I say: "May the Chinese people be able to consistently promote domestic goods, and may the Chinese people who promote domestic goods be able to enjoy wealth and honor to old age!"

Jiangnan University Basketball League Opening on March 6th this Season 163

Order of Play Scheduled and Announced

The Eighth Standing Committee of the Jiangnan University Basketball League met on the 25th of this month at the YMCA on Sichuan Road. Yu Jie, Wu Shijie, and Dong Xiaopei (representing Jiang Jingnan) were present. The following resolutions were passed:

Resolutions

(1) Men's and women's competitions will both adopt a single round-robin system.

(2) The winning team in each game will get two points, and the losing team will get zero points. If two or more teams have the same total score, there will be another competition to determine the championship. The method, date, location, referee, and other items will be determined by the committee.

(3) Men will use the 1934-35 rules, and women will use the women's basketball rules approved by the National Sports Advancement Association.

(4) Referees will be hired by the home team, but must be approved by the visiting team.

(5) In the event of rain, unsuitable playing conditions, or force majeure, the game may be rescheduled or played at another public location. In this case, the home team is responsible for notifying the visiting team and the committee, and obtaining consent. (Rescheduled games must be completed before April 1st.)

(6) If a team does not appear to play fifteen minutes after the scheduled game time, it will be considered a forfeit. However, this does not apply if the delay is caused by unforeseen circumstances en route.

(7) Team rosters must be submitted to Yu Jie of Zhenru Jinan University before March 6th.

(8) Each game time will be at 2:30 PM for women and 3:30 PM for men.

Twelfth World Games Location to be Voted on Tomorrow 165

Next Year's Berlin Conference

Football Program Passed

(Havas News Agency, Oslo, 26th) The International Olympic Committee will hold a plenary meeting this Friday to vote and decide on the location for the 1940 World Games. Tomorrow and Thursday, Italy, Japan, and Finland will each propose their capital cities as candidate locations for the 1940 World Games. At today's plenary meeting of the International Committee, the German representative reported on all the preparations for next year's Berlin World Games. In addition to all the programs from previous sessions, next year's World Games will include a football competition. According to the latest International Football Association, it is permitted to include football in the Olympic program, but with the condition that the participating teams should consist exclusively of players who are not paid salaries or rewards.

(Japan United Press, Oslo, 26th) The location for the 12th Olympic Games in 1940 will be decided on the final day of the committee, March 1st.

(Japan United Press, Oslo, 26th) The competition for the location of the Olympic Games is currently between Japan, Italy, and Finland, and the situation is chaotic, making predictions impossible. However, based on information from various sources, Japan is expected to receive a total of 22 votes, including those from the United States, Germany, Brazil, Canada, Czechoslovakia, Portugal, Australia, Sweden, India, and Mexico. The attitudes of Argentina, China, Chile, Peru, Cuba, Greece, Belgium, and Central American countries are still unclear. If these countries vote for Japan, Japan will have an absolute majority.

Ping City Cross-Country Race 166

Niu Qunzhi Wins Senior Group Championship

Luo Qinglong Lacks Endurance and is Defeated

(Beiping Correspondence) The Beiping City Cross-Country Race has been prepared for days by the Social Bureau, Public Security Bureau, and other departments and is now ready. The contestants from all parties participating in the competition gathered in front of Tiananmen Square one after another around 8:00 AM on the 24th. The sportswear worn by the participants varied, some wearing绒球 coats, some wearing vests, some wearing 灯笼裤, and some wearing shorts, showing no uniformity. At 9:45 AM, the Director of the Social Bureau arrived and shook hands with the athletes. Participants and spectators from all sides also arrived one after another, totaling about 500 people. First, Li Zhou reported the competition rules once. Then, everyone began taking photos. At 10:00 AM, the roll call was taken, and Commander Wang Zhensheng fired the starting gun. The contestants immediately began the race.

After hearing the gun, the contestants started together. The senior group headed east towards South Chizi, and the intermediate group headed west towards South Chang Street, going their separate ways. The spectators along the route were packed, and applause erupted. The atmosphere became tense as they passed various locations. At 10:30 AM, the intermediate group had already run out of Xisi Gate and past the Xisi Archway. As they reached the entrance to Huguosi Street, the senior group suddenly burst out from Huguosi Street. The leading general was Niu Qunzhi of the 32nd Army, and the entire team followed, running one after another.

The two groups accidentally met on the road, and the contestants competed with each other, striving to be first. At Xizhimen, traffic was temporarily stopped. At 10:40 AM, as the contestants were sweating and panting on the road, Luo Qinglong, a strong competitor from Tsinghua, suddenly surged from behind, leaping forward and passing everyone. At the same time, the Tsinghua cheering car also arrived, shouting "Ah Luo! Faster!" Luo Qinglong nodded and stepped up his efforts, sprinting ahead. About dozens of steps out of Xizhimen, the senior group changed course and turned north, heading straight for Tsinghua University. The intermediate group headed west, striving forward. He Chunbo of Huiwen College, with angry eyes and gritted teeth, was the first to reach the finish line at the Agricultural Experiment Field, taking about 32 minutes and 12 seconds. Fei Jingtian of Yuying College arrived second. A total of 32 members of the intermediate group reached the finish line one after another, with three dropping out midway.

As for the senior group, after leaving Xizhimen and turning north, Niu Qunzhi of the 32nd Army remained the vanguard. When he was about to reach Haidian, Niu Qunzhi charged forward like a fierce tiger leaving its cage, rushing far ahead. He reached the finish line in just one hour and ten minutes. Liu Qingling of Tsinghua arrived second. Luo Qinglong, although fast, lacked stamina and fell behind midway, finishing in 19th place, which is truly a pity. The names of the top 20 in the senior and intermediate groups are listed below:
